  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer3658066096619792825">Since his mother's death six years ago, Carter Kane has been living out of a suitcase, traveling the globe with his father, the brilliant Egyptologist, Dr. Julius Kane. But while Carter's been homeschooled, his younger sister, Sadie, has been living with their grandparents in London. Sadie has just what Carter wants—school friends and a chance at a "normal" life.   <span id="freeText3658066096619792825" style="display:none">Since his mother's death six years ago, Carter Kane has been living out of a suitcase, traveling the globe with his father, the brilliant Egyptologist, Dr. Julius Kane. But while Carter's been homeschooled, his younger sister, Sadie, has been living with their grandparents in London. Sadie has just what Carter wants—school friends and a chance at a "normal" life. But Carter has just what Sadie longs for—time with their father. After six years of living apart, the siblings have almost nothing in common. Until now.<br /><br />On Christmas Eve, Sadie and Carter are reunited when their father brings them to the British Museum, with a promise that he's going to "make things right." But all does not go according to plan: Carter and Sadie watch as Julius summons a mysterious figure, who quickly banishes their father and causes a fiery explosion.<br /><br />Soon Carter and Sadie discover that the gods of Ancient Egypt are waking, and the worst of them—Set—has a frightening scheme. To save their father, they must embark on a dangerous journey—a quest that brings them ever closer to the truth about their family and its links to the House of Life, a secret order that has existed since the time of the pharaohs.</span>

<div id="review_87088992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87088992" />
    <a title="Mitchel Broussard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2536904-mitchel-broussard"><img alt="Mitchel Broussard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577728446p2/2536904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87088992?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitchel Broussard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitchel Broussard" href="/user/show/2536904-mitchel-broussard">Mitchel Broussard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2536904-mitchel-broussard?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2536904-mitchel-broussard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87088992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11583864454521866113">Update: I've recently degraded this to a one star from a two when I realized how much of a disappointment it was. This review is, as a result, a lot more nicer than I'd like it to be. If you'd like, just add a lot more unnecessary cursing and asides about that idiotic taco-sauce showdown. *Sigh* Now I can't stop thinking about that goddamn battle anymore. Damn it.<br/><br/>If you're thinking "Oh it's just Percy Jackson with Egyptian Gods", you'd be correct. But, in it's own weird way, it's a bit more. At </span>
  <span id="freeText11583864454521866113" style="display:none">Update: I've recently degraded this to a one star from a two when I realized how much of a disappointment it was. This review is, as a result, a lot more nicer than I'd like it to be. If you'd like, just add a lot more unnecessary cursing and asides about that idiotic taco-sauce showdown. *Sigh* Now I can't stop thinking about that goddamn battle anymore. Damn it.<br /><br />If you're thinking "Oh it's just Percy Jackson with Egyptian Gods", you'd be correct. But, in it's own weird way, it's a bit more. At one point there's a little bit of Cassandra Clare's <i> Mortal Instruments </i>, some <i> Secrets of the Immortal Nicholas Flamel </i> by Michael Scott, and even a tad bit of <i> Harry Potter </i> thrown in. And, if you get though the first 200-300 pages you may enjoy yourself.<br /><br />Now is it worth having to get through that to find the good stuff? I'm not entirely sure. <br /><br />The set up is promising, as the two narrators (and protagonists) relay their plan to take an entire record of their adventure and then hide it in a locker and some school for the right person to find. If you read the opening chapter of <i> The Lightning Thief </i> and loved its warning, you'll thoroughly enjoy this. But it quickly became gimmicky to me, as Carter and Sadie take turns telling the tale, they also interrupt each other to crack awfully corny jokes and spout "witty" one liners. I think it would have been better to leave that narrative device to the opening and closing. Otherwise it distracts you from what is going on in the plot, which is quit more important than Sadie telling Carter how hilarious he was when a bird pooped on his face.<br /><br />And on the note of the characters, I'm all for alternating chapters between character perspectives, I've always loved it and find it highly effective as a way to open up the plot. But here, well, the characters speak a tad to similarly. I mean very early on Sadie uses her British accent heavily, but later in the book its almost completely gone, to the point where i had to check the top of the page to make sure i was reading a Sadie chapter. It wouldn't happen too often, but when it did i always felt a tinge of frustration. And it was always 2 Carter chapters, then 2 Sadie chapters. It seemed like an odd way to set everything up, why not just do 1:1?<br /><br />The only other thing that bothered me was the length. It took way too long to do what <i> The Lightning Thief </i> did in under 400 pages. Don't get me wrong, they do have fun battles, with a pretty cool magic system. But i found the battles went by too fast (one God they literally best by stuffing it with salsa so it turns into a cow. The most work Carter does is open huge vats of the hot Mexican sauce).<br /><br />On the positive side, Sadie and Carter do grow to respect one another and become pretty likable in the end. I still refuse to believe their age, 12 and 14? It just didn't fit their personalities to me, but i guess they're mature for their age.<br /><br />And on the reference above to all the other books, I'm not saying he copied from them, i simply meant there were similarities in story, characters and plot locations. Like the old church that Clary and her paranormal friends stay at in <i> City of Bones </i> is quite similar to the "First Nome" in this book. The twins from the Nicholas Flamel books have a similar relationship that Carter and Sadie have (albeit far more mature). And the magic system felt inspired by J.K. Rowling's famous teen magician, with similar uses of wands, the need to speak spells, and generally same types of spells (fire, wind, ice, light, etc).<br /><br />I guess the big question is will i read the sequels? And again, i'm forced to say I'm not entirely sure. There is a great twist in the end, and i'd love to see how it plays out and what happens. I most likely will, i just really hope they don't get progressively bigger. Unless it's stuffed with cool and lengthy battles, and a lot less stupid pre-teen distractions, i'm out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11583864454521866113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2402792705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2402792705" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2402792705?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=riordan-rick">riordan-rick</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2402792705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8396479742609094005">Not as good as Percy Jackson, Riordans´new series uses the same, great concept with reduced effort of the author to make it as great for all audiences as his Greek Roman mega world bestseller.<br/>The reasons:<br/><br/>Riordan could have simply invested more lifeblood, beta readers, and sweat in making this one the same thrilling, funny, and entertaining read as Percy Jackson, he should have already made enough money at this moment to be able to take some time for finetuning. It´s especially unnecessary that t</span>
  <span id="freeText8396479742609094005" style="display:none">Not as good as Percy Jackson, Riordans´new series uses the same, great concept with reduced effort of the author to make it as great for all audiences as his Greek Roman mega world bestseller.<br />The reasons:<br /><br />Riordan could have simply invested more lifeblood, beta readers, and sweat in making this one the same thrilling, funny, and entertaining read as Percy Jackson, he should have already made enough money at this moment to be able to take some time for finetuning. It´s especially unnecessary that the quality has been reduced, because the concept of using high plotted and detailed, well scripted and planned storylines, enabling many laughs and interconnections to make it seem much more coherent and vivid, really isn´t that much of a problem in that genre. It´s not as if it was high fantasy of hard sci-fi or something.<br /><br />I am missing the humor of the first series, it´s funny too, but not close as well executed and especially not aimed at all audiences at once, hidden innuendos for the adults and pure, clean fun for the kids. That´s coming in combination with the fact that it´s not that fast plotted, no tour de force of ideas and settings, and especially personifications of the ancient deities, letting the readers wonder how which god might appear in modern times. This kind of reminds me of Gaimans´ American Gods series that could have also lived up better to the expectations.<br /><br />Taking away or just reducing this element, the extra layer, the bonus dimension, of making it a bit brainier with hidden criticism and connotations, downgrades the whole thing to one´s average kids/YA read, nice and sweet and all, but nothing special anymore, just not the original, not the trademark Riordan was able to establish himself as.<br /><br />I am, of course, vivisecting it from the perspective of a strange kid in the body of an adult, so it might still be the perfect read for kids, teens, and real adults who aren´t into that meta analyzing anything to death and overcomplicated comparing it until it falls into pieces. It´s still a mess that Riordan deteriorated his perfect recept by diluting the ingredients that made it great for unknown, or the suggested, reasons. Remember Schlitz beer? It´s never a good idea to reduce the effort. <br /><br />And I don´t know another kids, YA author who didn´t deliver the same quality of got better and better, <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10896.Eoin_Colfer">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33467.Jonathan_Stroud">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/165168.Derek_Landy">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a><br />etc.<br />which makes it seem even stranger. <br /><br />Or maybe just the first part had exposition problems, it´s his only average novel, I just somehow subjectively and unscientifically didn´t really like the characters, and it will lift off with the second if one believes the meta rating scores? However, I am still totally looking forward towards reading the <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/82212-magnus-chase-and-the-gods-of-asgard">https://www.goodreads.com/series/8221...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/162088-the-trials-of-apollo">https://www.goodreads.com/series/1620...</a><br />series.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/TheKaneChronicles">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8396479742609094005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3530042459559518811">The Red Pyramid (Kane Chronicles #1), Rick Riordan<br/><br/>The Red Pyramid is a 2010 fantasy-adventure novel based on Egyptian mythology written by Rick Riordan. It is the first novel in The Kane Chronicles series. The novel was first published in the United States on May 4, 2010. <br/><br/>The novel opens with Carter and his father Julius Kane going to visit Carter's sister Sadie, who has lived with her maternal grandparents since the death of their mother, Ruby Kane. Julius, who is secretly a magician, but posin</span>
  <span id="freeText3530042459559518811" style="display:none">The Red Pyramid (Kane Chronicles #1), Rick Riordan<br /><br />The Red Pyramid is a 2010 fantasy-adventure novel based on Egyptian mythology written by Rick Riordan. It is the first novel in The Kane Chronicles series. The novel was first published in the United States on May 4, 2010. <br /><br />The novel opens with Carter and his father Julius Kane going to visit Carter's sister Sadie, who has lived with her maternal grandparents since the death of their mother, Ruby Kane. Julius, who is secretly a magician, but posing as a simple Egyptologist, takes the siblings to the British Museum, where he tries to bring Osiris (the Egyptian god of the Underworld) back into the mortal world. His magic also has the unintended side effect of summoning the gods Horus, Isis, Nephthys, and Set, as well as alerting the magicians Zia Rashid and Michel Desjardins to his actions, which are illegal in the magic community. <br /><br />Set, a god of chaos, captures Julius and destroys the museum. Unbeknownst to Carter and Sadie, each of the gods chooses a mortal host from the humans in the room. Carter and Sadie are taken to Brooklyn by their uncle Amos, who tells them they are descended from a long line of magicians, beginning with the Egyptian pharaohs Ramesses the Great and Narmer. He also explains the grave danger Set poses to the world, and goes to find him. While he is away, the mansion is attacked by Set's minions. With help from Sadie's cat Muffin, who is host to the goddess Bast, and Zia Rashid, they escape to Cairo. Once there, Carter and Sadie discover they are hosts to the gods Horus and Isis, respectively. <br /><br />They train in magic until the magicians' leader Iskandar dies and Michel Desjardins orders their deaths for collaborating illegally with the gods. The siblings escape and formulate a plan to defeat Set hoping to rescue their father and clear their names within the magic community. <br /><br />They travel to Set's lair in New Mexico, gathering ingredients for a magic spell and evading hostile monsters and magicians. Bast sacrifices herself while defending Carter and Sadie from Sobek; they encounter Amos and then Zia. <br /><br />The foursome heads to Set's hideout where they learn the final piece of the spell they need from a dying Zia, the unknowing host of Nephthys. Carter, Sadie, Horus, and Isis use the spell to subdue Set, although they stop short of completely destroying him because they realize his actions were dictated by a far worse enemy Apophis, a much more powerful god of chaos. Desjardins reluctantly allows Carter and Sadie to go free after they part with Horus and Isis. <br /><br />After a tearful goodbye with Zia, who turns out to have been a magical copy of the real young magician, Carter and Sadie return to Brooklyn. They visit their father, now in the underworld with their ghostly mother. As a gift, Osiris (hosted by the deceased Julius) helps Bast return to the mortal world. Carter and Sadie describe their plans to recruit other magicians to (illegally) study the path of the gods, while the former also resolves to seek out the real Zia Rashid.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و نهم سپتامبر سال 2016 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: هرم سرخ - کتاب 1 - سه گانه خاطرات خاندان کین؛ نویسنده ریک ریوردان؛ مترجم: آیدا کشوری؛ ویراستار فرزام حبیبی اصفهانی؛ تهران، بهنام، 1391؛ در 536 ص؛ از مجموعه خاطرات خاندان کین - کتاب اول؛ شابک: 9789645668936؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی سده 21 م<br /><br />عنوان: هرم سرخ - کتاب 1 - سه گانه وقایع نگاری کین؛ نویسنده: ریک ریوردان؛ مترجم: احمد محمدزاده؛ تهران، ای.بوک: پرشین بکس، 1391؛ در 396 ص؛<br /><br />این داستان در مورد زندگی: «سادی کین»؛ «کارتر کین»؛ و پدرشان است، که هر کدام قسمت هایی از داستان را روایت میکنند. داستان پس از ناپدید شدن پدر روی میدهد و آندو درمییابند که از اعضای خانواده ای قدیمی و مصری هستند، و مرگ مادرشان نیز به این موضوع ربط دارد. وقایع نگاری کین / جلد اول / هرم سرخ؛ اثر ریک ریوردن / مترجم: احمد محمدزاده؛ کارتر؛ فصل اول: مرگ در محل سوزن: ما فقط چند ساعت فرصت داریم، پس به دقت گوش کنید. اگر در حال شنیدن این داستان هستید، پس از حالا در خطرید. شاید من و سادی تنها شانس شما باشیم. به مدرسه بروید. قفسه را پیدا کنید؛ نمیگویم چه مدرسه ای یا چه قفسه ای، چون اگر شما همان فرد باشید پیدایش میکنید. رمز قفل 33/32/13 است وقتی همه ی ماجرا را شنیدید، معنای این شماره ها را خواهید فهمید. فقط به یاد داشته باشید داستانی که میخواهیم برایتان بازگو کنیم هنوز تمام نشده است و پایان آن به شما بستگی دارد؛ مهمترین نکته این است که بعد از باز کردن و دیدن محتویات آن، بسته را بیشتر از یک هفته نگه ندارید. مطمئنا،ً وسوسه کننده است. منظورم این است که قدرتی تقریباً نامحدود به شما میدهد. اما اگر برای مدتی طولانی آن را نگه دارید، شما را از پا میاندازد. رازهایش را کشف و آنرا برای نفر بعدی مخفی کنید؛ همانطور که من و سادی آن را برای شما مخفی کردیم. سپس خودتان را برای زندگی بسیار جالبی آماده کنید. بسیار خب، سادی میگوید سریعتر سر اصل مطلب بروم. خیلی خوب. فکر کنم از لندن و از شبی که پدرمان موزه ی بریتانیا را منفجر کرد، شروع شد. و ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2325213099?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423113454" href="/book/show/8700056-the-red-pyramid">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2325213099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5687926761071836254"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325213099' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Red Pyramid</a> ★★★★☆<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325213256' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Throne of Fire</a> ★★★☆☆<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325213397' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Serpent's Shadow</a> ★★★☆☆<br/><br/><b>“Fair means everyone gets what they need. And the only way to get what you need is to make it happen yourself.”</b></blockquote><br/>I grew up a huge fan of Egyptian mythology and history, plus I loved the <i>Percy Jackson and the Olympians</i> series when I <i>(finally)</i> picked it up a couple of years ago, so it was long overdue that I pick up the Kane Chronicles trilogy. I felt like I'd never heard of people raving about this series nearly as much</span>
  <span id="freeText5687926761071836254" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325213099" rel="nofollow noopener">The Red Pyramid</a> ★★★★☆<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325213256" rel="nofollow noopener">The Throne of Fire</a> ★★★☆☆<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325213397" rel="nofollow noopener">The Serpent's Shadow</a> ★★★☆☆<br /><br /><b>“Fair means everyone gets what they need. And the only way to get what you need is to make it happen yourself.”</b></blockquote><br />I grew up a huge fan of Egyptian mythology and history, plus I loved the <i>Percy Jackson and the Olympians</i> series when I <i>(finally)</i> picked it up a couple of years ago, so it was long overdue that I pick up the Kane Chronicles trilogy. I felt like I'd never heard of people raving about this series nearly as much as any of RR's other series, so I wasn't sure what to expect, but within just a few chapters of the audiobook for this one, I was so impressed! Sadie and Carter had such distinct, entertaining voices, I loved the banter and bickering between the two of them, and more than anything, I absolutely adored how quickly the two of them fell into these protective, caring sibling feelings for each other despite having been apart so much in their childhoods.<br /><br />While the plot itself felt rushed and convenient more than a few times, that's something I generally expect from a lot of MG books, so it didn't take away from my enjoyment too much. On the other hand, I really loved the casual representation with Sadie and Carter being biracial and the commentary on how Carter lived through so many different experiences than Sadie, with Carter being dark-skinned and Sadie being white-passing. <br /><br />I think the only big detractor from my enjoyment of this first installment was the weird, forced beginnings of romance here, which proved to be a big issue later in the series, sadly. I don't care for romance in MG novels to begin with, but especially romance as unnatural as the ships we see in this series. That said, they were minor in <i>The Red Pyramid,</i> so this first book still got an easy 4 stars from me!<br /><br />———<br /><br /><i>Buddy read with Ellyn!</i> ♥</span>

    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457347571?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457347571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12393820520874757469"><b>Buddy read with a few friends at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br/><br/>Rick Riodan (RR) is one of the few M.G. authors I read, I mean I’m in my 30s so usually a M.G. book isn’t going to hold my attention but RR is one of the few authors who can pull it off and does it well at that. What makes him special???? Well there are a few things that I really like about his writing. <br/><blockquote><br/>① - He writes teens like teens. They aren’t 12-16 year olds who act like they are in their 30s they are kids, behaving like kids. Carter </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12393820520874757469" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with a few friends at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br /><br />Rick Riodan (RR) is one of the few M.G. authors I read, I mean I’m in my 30s so usually a M.G. book isn’t going to hold my attention but RR is one of the few authors who can pull it off and does it well at that. What makes him special???? Well there are a few things that I really like about his writing. <br /><blockquote><br />① - He writes teens like teens. They aren’t 12-16 year olds who act like they are in their 30s they are kids, behaving like kids. Carter and Sadie argue like real siblings would and I totally enjoyed their interactions and teasing of each other.<br /><br />② - Action….Action….Action. Seriously there is always something happening. The stories move along quickly with chases, fights and discovery scenes everywhere. There are lots of clues along the way and some of them can be misleading until you get to the big picture of it all.<br /><br />③ - The mythology used is fantastic and so well thought out. I love RR’s interpretation of the Egyptian gods, magic and lore. There is a new interesting interpretation of them and how they interact with the world. It is new and exciting and I really loved how it was all shown and explained.<br /><br />④ - The magic and world building. I get so upset when reading a book and not understanding how powers work. I don’t care if it takes a little while to roll it out but I NEED to understand it. I want to feel like if I lived in this world I too could do magic. <i>I’m still convinced I would have done as well as Hermione at Hogwarts if I got an invitation.</i> So I appreciate it when authors incorporate learning how to use the magic in their story. After this book I was sure I could do the magic of this world if I was in it.<br /><br />⑤ - Interesting cohesive story and plotting that lend to a bang up conclusion. RR totally has a good voice and knows where his story is going. I never feel at the end that he has just thrown something in at last minute to fix everything. It is a fantastic trait to have in a story teller.<br /></blockquote><br />There are a ton of reviews on this so I’ll just say Sadie and Carter were separated and raised apart after the death of their mother six years ago. But now through a series of events they are thrown together and must find a way to work with one another to save their father. With the help of a few unusual friends they must find ways to unlock the Power of the Gods (Egyptian ones) within themselves and try to save the world. Easy peasy….if they can quit squabbling long enough.<br /><br />If you add a few Gods, an albino crocodile, a cat named muffin, some spunky clay creations, a secret magical society and an orangutan with some special dietary needs together and shake you come up with one hell of a good time.<br /><br />I liked the Percy Jackson stories just a tad better but if you like mythology then this could be a great time for you too.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12393820520874757469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965189835" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965189835?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423113454" href="/book/show/8700056-the-red-pyramid">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965189835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12654404319343968801"><i>
  <blockquote>“It takes strength and courage to admit the truth.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Honestly, who does it better than Rick Riordan when it comes to middle-grade fantasy books? The answer is no one. He never ceases to amaze me with the ideas he's coming up with, and although one could say that his books and ideas are being recycled I downright disagree with that notion. He's written about the Greek Gods, about the Roman Gods and then the Egyptian Gods, and each time he comes up with completely different ideas and twists to e</span>
  <span id="freeText12654404319343968801" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“It takes strength and courage to admit the truth.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Honestly, who does it better than Rick Riordan when it comes to middle-grade fantasy books? The answer is no one. He never ceases to amaze me with the ideas he's coming up with, and although one could say that his books and ideas are being recycled I downright disagree with that notion. He's written about the Greek Gods, about the Roman Gods and then the Egyptian Gods, and each time he comes up with completely different ideas and twists to encase his stories in.<br /><br />Carter and Sadie Kane are two siblings, they've never seen much of each other since their mother died and their father took custody of Carter (the eldest) whereas Sadie was taken under their grandparents' care. <br /><br />Carter is that smart, humble kid, who's always there to help and Sadie is that outgoing, sassy girl you were classmates with when you were in elementary school. <br /><br />And now, let's fast forward to the part where the Egyptian Gods are unleashed and they find shelter in human hosts. Amongst these Gods, there is the worst of them, the God of Chaos, Set who's hell bent upon destroying the world.<br /><br />So, the kids learn who they are (which is for you to find out... I mean, were their parents Gods? Or are they Gods themselves? Or maybe they're just common humans trying to save the world?)<br /><br />You may think you're a little too familiar with this storyline, especially if you're an avid Riordan reader, but you'll be up for a surprise, trust me.<br /><br />This somehow felt a lot more fast-paced than all of his other books. Usually, Mr. Riordan takes his time with the characters and the plot but in this one everything was faster than usual and I admit that I loved the change.<br /><br />I'm saving my five stars for the next book, this was just shy of getting it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12654404319343968801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_99272132" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99272132" />
    <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent"><img alt="Aaron Vincent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360133074p2/2924544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99272132?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Vincent" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent">Aaron Vincent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=ya-mg-fantasy">ya-mg-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99272132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5340270447200993479">I ranked Rick Riordan's The Lighting Thief 5th on my Top Ten Fave Books for 2009, tied with Michael Scott's The Alchemist. I reasoned out that I can't choose which one is better cause both made learning history fun and both have that cool factor reliving the things in the past. Now, I have suspicion that I unknowingly can see the future cause The Red Pyramid is exactly the combination of both books. Is that a good thing? Yes, if it had been well executed. Let's review that sentence: "Yes, if it </span>
  <span id="freeText5340270447200993479" style="display:none">I ranked Rick Riordan's The Lighting Thief 5th on my Top Ten Fave Books for 2009, tied with Michael Scott's The Alchemist. I reasoned out that I can't choose which one is better cause both made learning history fun and both have that cool factor reliving the things in the past. Now, I have suspicion that I unknowingly can see the future cause The Red Pyramid is exactly the combination of both books. Is that a good thing? Yes, if it had been well executed. Let's review that sentence: "Yes, if it <b>had been</b> well executed." Yeah, as what my stars above says<i>(don't look up to the sky dumbass, I mean the rating stars.)</i>, it is not an awesome book. <br /><br />Its given that Egyptian History is not as fascinating as the Greek and Roman History but egyptian culture has that sense of mystery that Riordan could have played. I didn't get the Egyptian feel to it at all. The existence of the egyptian gods in the book is not that cool either. Thoth playing Rock Band is not as cool as Ares riding the Big Bike or Horus being cranky is not as funny as Dionysius being stubborn. The whole god thing is like just for the sake of having them. You can substitute them with normal people's name and would have still the same effect. The spells are cool. The thing about glowing hieroglyphs after saying the spell is brilliant but I can't see "Ha-di" replacing "Alohomora" for young people getting locked out when they go home late<i> (It's pretty easy to guess why I know this.)</i><br /><br />The storyline even gets repetitive:<br /><br />Sadie and Caine goes to one place.<br />They start bickering. [Shut up, Sadie and Carter! It's my review:]<i>(Read the book to get the sarcasm.)</i><br />One of them falls asleep and their soul drifts somewhere.<br />Enemy attacks them.<br />They fight<i>(a little)</i>.<br />Their company fights alone to buy time for them while they run.<br />They eventually be reunited with that someone.<br /><br /><br />The whole recording thing is distracting most of the times especially the [:] remarks. It would have been better if it's only on the beginning and the end just like in the Lightning Thief.<br /><br />As for the main characters, Sadie and Carter is the least likable sibling I ever read. They are not awesome nor annoying, they are just blah. Forgettable. They continuously throw corny jokes and weak sarcasms. And at some point, their voice on the chapters gets confusing. I have to look up to the top of the page to be sure who is talking. Even towards the end, I still didn't get what kind of personality they have. <br /><br />Now I am unsure if I will still follow this series. Maybe if Riordan will able to redeem himself on The Last Hero(a book that tells about something he is really good at), I will read the second installment for the Kane Chronicles to make up for the time while waiting for the second Heroes of Olympus book. Don't worry Rick Riordan, I still like you and I understand that you, like every writers out there, sometimes just needs the pay check. Peace' :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5340270447200993479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97791388" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97791388" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446509-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194659951p2/446509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97791388?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/446509-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=actionadventure">actionadventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97791388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3565224047168023293">I quite enjoyed Riordan's new adventures featuring the Kane siblings, Carter and Sadie (I believe 14 and 12 years of age... though I thought Sadie seemed older), who are introduced to the possibilities that Egyptian mythology may be a bit more real than they realized.<br/><br/>Sadie and Carter's mother died when they were young, and since then they have had to live apart - Sadie with her mother's parents in London, and Carter with his father, traveling the world looking for Egyptian artifacts. Since they </span>
  <span id="freeText3565224047168023293" style="display:none">I quite enjoyed Riordan's new adventures featuring the Kane siblings, Carter and Sadie (I believe 14 and 12 years of age... though I thought Sadie seemed older), who are introduced to the possibilities that Egyptian mythology may be a bit more real than they realized.<br /><br />Sadie and Carter's mother died when they were young, and since then they have had to live apart - Sadie with her mother's parents in London, and Carter with his father, traveling the world looking for Egyptian artifacts. Since they only see each other once a year or so, it nicely adds to the story to have their relationship develop and evolve.<br /><br />When visiting the museum something goes terrible wrong, and Carter and Sadie discover that there may be more to their father, and the Kane family, than they realized.<br /><br />I listened to the audio book, which I thought was wonderful! It is narrated by Kevin R. Free and Katherine Kellgren. Because the story is told both by Carter and Sadie, each narrator reads the appropriate section. The book is very suited to an audio recording, as it is supposed to be Carter and Sadie making a recording of the events that have transpired. <br /><br />I enjoy the Percy Jackson books, and I think that this book has a similar style, a similar since of fun and lightness, but happily it didn't feel the same, like I was reading the same story just with differently named characters. To me, Red Pyramid felt a little more mature and complex (not in a bad way, just in that the protagonists are older, there's more history, details, etc.). I enjoyed this, and - like the Percy Jackson books with Greek mythology - The Red Pyramid made me intrigued with Egyptian mythology and history (the author's note, by the way, is fantastic!).<br /><br />Also, it was very nice and refreshing to have the Kane siblings be mixed race, with a black father and white mother. Not only does this bring about some interesting sibling points (since Carter is darker and Sadie lighter they are often not perceived to be brother and sister) but I also thought Riordan handled it all really well, not making a big deal about, letting the story still be the story, but with a few mentions here and there where this is mentioned. <br /><br />I'm hoping that there will be more to this series, and I'm anxiously awaiting reading the rest - I mean, what's not to love with dueling avatar half-man-half-bird forms, wands and staffs, and a protective cat?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3565224047168023293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_194098553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194098553" />
    <a title="Priscilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731097-priscilla"><img alt="Priscilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451806103p2/4731097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194098553?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Priscilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Priscilla" href="/user/show/4731097-priscilla">Priscilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194098553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12416057707309165693">Such a fun, entertaining read! <br/><br/>Initial thoughts:<br/>1. Interactive with the reader. Riordon pulls you into the story!<br/>2. Amazing Egyptian mythology! Gods, and magic everything!<br/>3. Elements that remind me of Percy Jackson and Harry Potter. Didn't bother me, but it's noteworthy.<br/>4. Full of banter, and sarcasm. Loved it!<br/>5. Action-packed, and fast paced! Lot's of story but it's filled with something insane.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=n2O9n2EV5ww' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out my full book video review!</a></span>
  <span id="freeText12416057707309165693" style="display:none">Such a fun, entertaining read! <br /><br />Initial thoughts:<br />1. Interactive with the reader. Riordon pulls you into the story!<br />2. Amazing Egyptian mythology! Gods, and magic everything!<br />3. Elements that remind me of Percy Jackson and Harry Potter. Didn't bother me, but it's noteworthy.<br />4. Full of banter, and sarcasm. Loved it!<br />5. Action-packed, and fast paced! <div id="review_262927719" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262927719" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4265643-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585543407p2/4265643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262927719?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/4265643-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4265643-natalie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4265643-natalie?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4265643-natalie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262927719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7492726953153289342">I hate when this happens. I see it all the time.<br/>Great writer writes book. Book gets discovered, gets really famous. Writer makes a billion copies of said book in deteriorating quality.<br/>Rick Riordan should've stuck to his Percy Jackson series and his sister-series to that. Instead, I can see the dollar-signs in his eyes and the mocking "cha-ching!" in the background, and here we have the Kane Chronicles.<br/>Part of the reason I enjoyed The Lightning Thief so much is because the insight and dialogue we</span>
  <span id="freeText7492726953153289342" style="display:none">I hate when this happens. I see it all the time.<br />Great writer writes book. Book gets discovered, gets really famous. Writer makes a billion copies of said book in deteriorating quality.<br />Rick Riordan should've stuck to his Percy Jackson series and his sister-series to that. Instead, I can see the dollar-signs in his eyes and the mocking "cha-ching!" in the background, and here we have the Kane Chronicles.<br />Part of the reason I enjoyed The Lightning Thief so much is because the insight and dialogue were very true to a teenage boy. Awkward, confused, and with the emotional range of a teaspoon, yet he still had the depth of a good and likable character. <br />The Red Pyramid switches dialogue between a sister and brother, Sadie and Carter, in which he drops the awkward dialogue, picking up a sort of vague, non-specific voice for both of the characters.<br />I hate switching POVs unless it's done VERY well, and the problem is, most people who are good at creating voices don't switch. Because they're smart, unlike these sorry souls. <br />And if you're going to feel the need to switch POVs, have some sort of difference between the two, ESPECIALLY if you're going to mention how unlike the two characters are every bloody second. If they're so different, how do they have the exact same dull voice?<br /><br />Also, I found the characters themselves dull, just like their vocal counterparts. Sadie had no depth at all- she just acted bored, snarky or confused and helpless. While the Lightning Thief's characters might have been slightly cliche, that's something I could get past. I just snoozed through the whole book. Carter was pretty much as bad. <br /><br />The plot was already used; I liked the whole son-needs-to-save-mom thing in the Lightning Thief, but you can't just use it twice! Also, in The Lightning Thief, Riordan spent time nurturing and explaining the relationship between Percy and his mom, so you actually cared when she got captured. Honestly, I didn't give a flying ankh whether Mr. Kane lived or died. Frankly, by the end <i>I</i> wanted to be crushed by a Rosetta Stone. Plus, as they explained so well, Sadie didn't even know her dad. <br /><br />The plot itself was used and meaningless, and the characters bored me to tears. And there was no Leo Valdez or random minor god to crack me up either, I mean seriously. Go do yourself a favor and buy Les Miserables, it's funnier.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7492726953153289342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435084507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4580612391040244534">Let me confess something before I start my review: I dived in this book with lower than zero expectations. My sister has read them and she kind of hinted at them not being as good as the PJO series so I was very hard on the story. Thus, the three stars. I mean, I went in to hate the characters -which I kind of did- but overall, how could I even think about hating a Rick Riordan book?<br/><br/>The Red Pyramid, is sort of similar to other Rick books but had its own special moments. For one, it was about Egy</span>
  <span id="freeText4580612391040244534" style="display:none">Let me confess something before I start my review: I dived in this book with lower than zero expectations. My sister has read them and she kind of hinted at them not being as good as the PJO series so I was very hard on the story. Thus, the three stars. I mean, I went in to hate the characters -which I kind of did- but overall, how could I even think about hating a Rick Riordan book?<br /><br />The Red Pyramid, is sort of similar to other Rick books but had its own special moments. For one, it was about Egyptian Gods. One of the reasons I didn't really enjoy this story -which is my fault, not the book's- is because my knowledge of the Egyptian Gods was Zero. In result, I had a hard time having fun because I was busy figuring out the Gods.<br /><br />My second problem is that I didn't like the characters, Sadie in particular. Which is again me, not the book.<br /><br />But in the end, everything was fast-paced and the plot was interesting. I also liked they were kind of narrating the story as a recording. <br /><br />I'm going to continue with this serious and try to be less of a judgmental asshole. Hopefully, I will have more fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4580612391040244534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1353358878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353358878" />
    <a title="Jesica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44637869-jesica"><img alt="Jesica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469336667p2/44637869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353358878?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesica" href="/user/show/44637869-jesica">Jesica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353358878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14814053051709652931"><blockquote>“Fairness does not mean everyone gets the same,” Dad said. “Fairness means everyone gets what they need. And the only way to get what you need is to make it happen yourself. Do you understand?”</blockquote><br/>I always adore Rick Riordan’s ability to turn odd and boring mythologies into fun stories. The first I read was the famous <i>Percy Jackson and The Olympians</i> series. Basically this series has a lot of similarities to Percy Jackson series only it’ a Egypt instead of Greek and magicians instead of demigods. Of </span>
  <span id="freeText14814053051709652931" style="display:none"><blockquote>“Fairness does not mean everyone gets the same,” Dad said. “Fairness means everyone gets what they need. And the only way to get what you need is to make it happen yourself. Do you understand?”</blockquote><br />I always adore Rick Riordan’s ability to turn odd and boring mythologies into fun stories. The first I read was the famous <i>Percy Jackson and The Olympians</i> series. Basically this series has a lot of similarities to Percy Jackson series only it’ a Egypt instead of Greek and magicians instead of demigods. Of course there were silly gods and goddesses too but the magicians didn’t worship them, they feared and fought them.<br /><br />This first book of the series tells of Carter and Sadie Kane, brother and sister, who found out that they were magicians after their father, magician too, performed a forbidden spell and accidently freed five most powerful Egyptian gods. Osiris, Horus, Isis, Nephtys, and Set. Carter and Sadie then were brought to a magician organization in Egypt, The House of Life, where they found out that they had involuntary each hosted one of the escaped gods, Horus and Isis. So Carter and Sadie escaped the house od life with the minimum magic they had learned, two not-so-helpful Egyptian gods inside their heads and their pet cat Muffin/the cat goddess, set off to save their lives and prevent the evil god, Set, to build The Red Pyramid and started the end of the world.<br /><br />The story, though I can’t say it’s original since it has a lot of similarities to Rick Riordan’s own other books, was quite exciting. The writing style is fun. It’s a first person POV like so many books, but it was funny how it’s like Carter and Sadie sent to Rick Riordan to write their recorded message about their adventure so other young magicians could read.<br /><blockquote><b>WARNING</b><br />The following is a transcript of a digital recording. In certain places, the audio quality was poor, so some words and phrases represent the author’s best guesses. Where possible, illustrations of important symbols mentioned in the recording have been added. Background noises such as scuffling, hitting, and cursing by the two speakers have not been transcribed. The author makes no claims for the authenticity of the recording. It seems impossible that the two young narrators are telling the truth, but you, the reader, must decide for yourself.</blockquote><br />In the end, it’s a really fun narration with sometimes some funny squabbles between the two narrators. Both Sadie and Carter had their own unique personalities and style and they complemented each other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14814053051709652931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9962513965873600125">hmmm.. I guess if you haven't read Percy Jackson, you'll definitely LOVE this book! It is enjoying to read! Rick Riordan is absolutely humorous! Writing in two different perspectives is really not easy, so thumbs up to him for that! <br/><br/>BUT! there's just a few 'but's since i'm an avid fan of Percy Jackson. i didn't quite enjoy it as i thought i would. it's just waaaay too similar to percy jackson. like percy jackson, they're also looking for children with pharaoh blood and everything. and like percy</span>
  <span id="freeText9962513965873600125" style="display:none">hmmm.. I guess if you haven't read Percy Jackson, you'll definitely LOVE this book! It is enjoying to read! Rick Riordan is absolutely humorous! Writing in two different perspectives is really not easy, so thumbs up to him for that! <br /><br />BUT! there's just a few 'but's since i'm an avid fan of Percy Jackson. i didn't quite enjoy it as i thought i would. it's just waaaay too similar to percy jackson. like percy jackson, they're also looking for children with pharaoh blood and everything. and like percy, the main characters carter and sadie lived in the shadow all throughout their lives but found out the truth later on when they have to save the world from Set. <br /><br />BUT again, i still loved the book. It's interesting since it involves Egyptian gods and goddesses and their rich culture. Ancient Egyptian culture had always intrigued me when I was young and it is great to find a book about it, even greater to know that Rick Riordan's the author. I learned a lot in reading this book. It IS a good book on its own. I absolutely recommend it especially if you haven't read Percy Jackson yet. <br /><br />although it's just my opinion. :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11652321027392744048">You know that I am a mythology sucker. I love mythology! Every single time that I read about it or watch something with mythology I'm like:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/418292.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Besides,Egyptian mythology particularly fascinates me, so I could only love The Kane Chronicles! :) <br/>Though I must say that Carter really pissed me off sometimes.   <span id="freeText11652321027392744048" style="display:none">You know that I am a mythology sucker. I love mythology! Every single time that I read about it or watch something with mythology I'm like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/418292.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Besides,Egyptian mythology particularly fascinates me, so I could only love The Kane Chronicles! :) <br>Though I must say that Carter really pissed me off sometimes. He still didn't grow on me like Percy did.<br>I could immediately connect with Percy but with Carter that didn't happen. I didn't like when, in the beginning, he said that he was fine with being with his sister only twice a year. <br>I mean, my sister is <s> the freaking devil's personification </s> a little bit difficult child but, still, I love her and I would be very sad if I could be with her only twice a year and we were pratically strangers to each other.<br>I also didn't like when he thought that they had nothing in common and that Sadie never acted normal and that she was stupid. And I really hated when he thought that Sadie was the lucky one because she was left behind while he was travelling around the world with this freaking father! Yeah, it must be really difficult to be with the only parent you've left, constantly travelling, while your sister is in the other side of the world, feeling rejected and alone! :S<br>I was really really like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372602ra/725938.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But whatever, I prospered. I got through that. I like Carter but he has to make me forget this stuff.<br>About Sadie - OMG, she's hilarious! I would love to have a 12 year-old sister like that! :)<br>Like I said, I really connected with her. She was the one who suffered the most with everything that happened to her family. I mean, I wouldn't take it easy as well if my mother died and then my father and my elder brother left me alone. I feel so sorry for her. :(<br>And I hope that she ends up with Anubis. +.+ I really loved Anubis! My reaction when I was reading about him was the same reaction Sadie had when she first saw him: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372602ra/725939.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7978291200478215314"><b>3.5 Golden Stars</b><br/><br/>RTC after re-read<br/><br/>maybe this series is my least favourite among all the Riordan's series & in the whole Riordanverse, maybe it's because Egypt myths is my least favourite mythology (I found it very complicated & dry), maybe this book is my least favourite in the series.<br/>but it doesn't mean I don't love them.   <span id="freeText7978291200478215314" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Golden Stars</b><br /><br />RTC after re-read<br /><br />maybe this series is my least favourite among all the Riordan's series &amp; in the whole Riordanverse, maybe it's because Egypt myths is my least favourite mythology (I found it very complicated &amp; dry), maybe this book is my least favourite in the series.<br />but it doesn't mean I don't love them. Just my love is lesser than PJO, HoO, ToA &amp; MCGA. but I still love them &amp; the whole series is a 5 stars.<br /><br />Meet the Kane siblings to enter the Kane chronicles: Carter &amp; Sadie<br />They are totally different, one is book-smart, one is badass &amp; sarcastic, they were separated since their mother's death, Carter's been living out of a suitcase with his father who was Egyptologist; he is calm, leader-like &amp; loves books, Sadie living in London with her grandparents &amp; she is stubborn &amp; saucy. See? the siblings have almost nothing in common, until now. *suspense music in distance*<br />Soon Carter and Sadie discover that the gods of Ancient Egypt are waking, and the worst of them—Set—has a frightening scheme. they entered the world of myths so suddenly &amp; unexpectedly, going on a dangerous journey, a quest that brings them ever closer to the truth about their family and its links to the House of Life, a secret order that has existed since the time of the pharaohs.<br />many cool characters &amp; awesome villains; like always.<br /><br />beginning was great &amp; exciting, but in the middle it was slow (or I was out of Riordanverse mode &amp; not reading it for a while), but then again, the exciting parts begin soon enough.<br /><br />Fun! you can't expect you simply read an uncle Rick's book not laughing your heart out! the sibling relationship between these two are awesome. I love them.<br />Carter is my favourite character &amp; Sadie is very cool. I kinda like her. (tho sometimes she's rude, but all's good)<br />the writing style was perfect, the way they grabbing each other's turn to tell the story adding spiced-fun up to the never-ending fun. XD<br />the World building, a bit dry, but also perfectly wrapping up in the reality, like always.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9266332559587534404"><b> actual rating: 3.5/5 stars </b> <br/><br/><br/><b>It takes strength and courage to admit the truth. </b> <br/><br/><b> Plot: </b> Well this one was interesting but i also found it very lacking in that i didn't connect with these characters or story in anyway which is disappointing. This story follows the two different perspectives of Sadie and Carter Kane who both living in different countries and different lives for them to come together when their dad is taken away from them. <br/><br/>I did find it a little difficult at times to try and sepera</span>
  <span id="freeText9266332559587534404" style="display:none"><b> actual rating: 3.5/5 stars </b> <br /><br /><br /><b>It takes strength and courage to admit the truth. </b> <br /><br /><b> Plot: </b> Well this one was interesting but i also found it very lacking in that i didn't connect with these characters or story in anyway which is disappointing. This story follows the two different perspectives of Sadie and Carter Kane who both living in different countries and different lives for them to come together when their dad is taken away from them. <br /><br />I did find it a little difficult at times to try and seperate the two main characters and have two different voices inside my head but it did help with Sadie growing up and living in England so the different language at times did help. One thing that really did stand out for me and in all of Rick's books is how much humour is such a massive part of how these characters interact and it's one thing that i love from these books. <br /><br /><br />The Egyptian history and magic was all very interesting to me because i've never learned about this type of history and i'm glad that it was told in this type of story to make it enjoyable to read and also learn some new facts. <br /><br /><br />Out of the two i think in this book Sadie was the one to shine out more on the page than Carter did and i know this book is setting up the next adventure so theres still time for me to get to know these two but i still stand by Sadie coming through more as the better character for this one. <br /><br /><br />However there was just something that was missing from this book and i think it lasted all throughout the book for me, the first half of the book was a little slow and hard to get into but once things picked up i found my rhythm and got with the story. I did find the characters really harder to like going into this one and i'm not going to compare any of the characters from Percy Jackson or the Heroes of Olympus because all the characters are different and unique in their own ways however i just had trouble connecting to these characters and i have no idea why. <br /><br /><br />Overall this story was enjoyable for the most part and i will continue with the rest of the series because towards the end is where i really started to get into this story so i'm hoping that book two picks up with a more stronger story. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer734201081097982613">GAAAHHHHH!!! Well, you know I only start a review that way if I'm really mad or if I'm really excited. In this case, it's the latter. :)<br/><br/>I am a huuuuge fan of Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson & the Olympian series, and those of you who love those will enjoy his new Kane Chronicles, too. I was a little nervous at first, thinking it wouldn't be as awesome, but after reading The Red Pyramid I don't feel the need to compare the two. There were some similar elements––Egyptian gods instead of Greek gods, a</span>
  <span id="freeText734201081097982613" style="display:none">GAAAHHHHH!!! Well, you know I only start a review that way if I'm really mad or if I'm really excited. In this case, it's the latter. :)<br /><br />I am a huuuuge fan of Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympian series, and those of you who love those will enjoy his new Kane Chronicles, too. I was a little nervous at first, thinking it wouldn't be as awesome, but after reading The Red Pyramid I don't feel the need to compare the two. There were some similar elements––Egyptian gods instead of Greek gods, a lot of traveling to random places, both a lot of action and a lot of humor. But there are unique traits to each series, and I can see myself getting just as attached to this new series as I am to PJO.<br /><br />The only thing I had issues with was the believability about the whole thing being a tape recording. I mean, it was cute with the little parentheses notes, like (Ow! Sadie kicked me!). But other than that it didn't really read like someone "talking". It was one of those things like Interview with the Vampire (only that was even worse because the entire thing was actually written in quotation marks …), like "Okay. No one talks that way." But, whatever. At least it was an interesting idea.<br /><br />Over all––great new story, awesome characters, exciting and hilarious and all those other good things. Hooray for Rick Riordan! *applauds*</span>
  <a data-text-id="734201081097982613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2764583430" class="readable"
